[1] Part 1 - 1985 Winter
[2] Origins of the Legend - Transcription
[3] This was over a thousand years ago. The elderly couple, the founders of the village, discovered a hot spring bubbling up from the mountains. From the spring emerged a girl. The couple, childless, took care of the girl with great care.
[4] Soon, the daughter grew up to be a beautiful woman. A dragon appeared, causing a flood in the village. The daughter possessed an incredible power, suppressing the dragon's movements. However, she did not completely eliminate the dragon, so the flood continued every four years.
[5] The daughter's strength and beauty were highly praised. Shortly thereafter, numerous people from all over the world came to ask for her hand in marriage after hearing the legend. The daughter gave them a challenge, saying she would choose a husband who held the Penglai zither. However, no one succeeded. Although there were those who brought counterfeit instruments, the daughter's touch immediately broke the strings. However, a man from the east overcame great difficulties and finally succeeded. The daughter married him as promised.
[6] Soon after, the couple had a daughter, named Qiyao. Qiyao grew up and possessed even greater power than her mother. When the dragon returned, Qiyao played the Penglai zither, and the sound of the zither cut off the dragon's head, neatly eliminating the dragon. At the same time, the Penglai zither that had fulfilled its mission was broken into two pieces.
[7] The villagers were surprised and asked the daughter why she could accomplish what her mother could not. The mother answered that although she inherited a large amount of power from the gods, it was not enough to eliminate another god. It was only because Qiyao mixed excellent human blood that she could eliminate the dragon. Although Qiyao only inherited half of her mother's power, she inherited her father's entire power. To eliminate the dragon, the power of the gods and human power were both necessary.
[8] At the age of forty, Qiyao passed her title to her daughter and descended to become an ordinary person. The daughter also inherited half of her mother's power and all of human power. Although Qiyao had a son, he could only inherit half of his mother's power and not his father's, so he could not succeed Qiyao's position. Moreover, Qiyao said that if the person who could best inherit her power inherited her legacy, the village would be long-lasting.
[9] Since then, the Qiyao family has had female descendants inherit their power and have properly governed the village. This is the current Qiyao family.
[10] * * *
[11][1] God era: In Japanese mythology, it refers to the era before Emperor Jimmu ascended the throne, i.e., the mythical era.
[12] 1
[13] Shōta Hosono visited the hot spring of Penglai for the second time. The first time was two years ago. He had an old-fashioned hobby of traveling to hot springs, so he and his university friend got along well. During the winter break of two years ago, they spent an entire month wandering around a cold, obscure hot spring resort in the Shinshū region. Their trip was quite modest, and they earned their travel expenses by working at various destinations. They carefully investigated travel guide magazines and chose cheap yet seemingly pleasant inns to stay at. Although they occasionally hitchhiked when they were short on money, food was the only exception, and they insisted on having dishes with a certain level of quality.
[14] They had endured many hardships such as getting rained on and walking for two hours, but it was precisely because of this that their satisfaction was particularly strong and had become a beautiful memory of their lives. After walking nearly twenty hot spring resorts, the hot spring they visited on the eve of the end of their trip was Penglai.
[15] Penglai was a small hot spring inn, so it was not listed in any travel guides. Initially, they had no intention of visiting it, but their plan changed suddenly when the innkeeper of the inn they stayed at the previous night mentioned a secret hot spring that was unknown to the public. Penglai was not only the hot spring inn but also the village of Hikari, which was unknown. The rough map of the travel guide did not even write the village name, but only drew two lines in front of the triangular mark indicating the mountain top, one of which was a river and the other was a road that abruptly ended.
[16] "This place is a hidden gem," said the friend, grinning.
[17] However, when they arrived in Yamauchi Village after several bus transfers, they were surprised to find that it was even smaller than they had imagined. The village, nestled in a low-lying valley surrounded by steep mountains, was sparsely populated with scattered houses. The river flowing through the village divided it in two, with only a small patch of flat land on which rice paddies and terraced fields were laid out. The two hills on either side approached from above, their snow-capped peaks obscuring the sky. They got off the bus and asked a local for directions. The villager looked at them curiously and pointed upstream along the river. When they asked for an explanation, the villager said that although a few tourists came to the hot spring for healing, they all drove there. It was only natural, as the road to the inn was not accessible by public transportation, and Kenji Maeda and his friend had to hike for about thirty minutes with their backpacks.
[18] That's all the impression Kenji Maeda has of Kotoyu Onsen from two years ago. He remembers the route well, but he can't recall the exact structure of the inn or the outdoor hot spring. Everything was old and well-maintained, but there were no other guests, so the atmosphere was excellent – that's all that remains in his foggy memory. Despite the hot spring and inn being good, they didn't leave a lasting impression. Since it's a small village, there were no opportunities to work, so they left hastily after staying for just one night. This is why the memory is vague. The run-down hot spring inn was far from being a gold mine.
[19] Therefore, just a month ago, Kotoyu Onsen was almost forgotten by Kenji Maeda. He suddenly remembered Kotoyu Onsen because of the old story the innkeeper told him.
[20] "Where are you going today, Mr. Kenji Maeda?"
[21] Jumon was about to leave the inn when the innkeeper, Jidai Kouzawa, politely approached him. He was a rough-looking mountain man of about thirty-five years old, but his tone and attitude were quite gentle.
[22] His feet were wrapped around a pet called Tsuki. Tsuki was a pure white snowy weasel about twenty centimeters long, with only the tip of its tail black. Last year, it was found injured in a stone mortar in the town of Yachiyo and was named Tsuki. It was said that snowy weasels were wary animals, but perhaps it was because Jidai took care of it when it was still young, so it was very docile and friendly. It is now kept as a mascot of Otofu.
[23] "I'm going to see the Dragon's Head again."
[24] "The Dragon's Head, huh…"
[25] Kouzawa showed a "again?" expression. It was also understandable, as Jumon had been going to the Dragon's Head for the past four days.
[26] Quiet Horse had been staying here for three days. It was not a place where a young man of twenty would typically spend much time alone. To avoid suspicion, Quiet Horse had used the excuse that he was conducting field research for his graduation thesis, but it was unclear whether Kichijiro had any suspicions. Although Kichijiro mentioned that scholars occasionally visited the place, it was possible that he frequently approached Quiet Horse to monitor his activities.
[27] "But isn't there anything that needs to be investigated so much in such a secluded place?"
[28] "Hmm, it's for field research, kind of like a graduation practice."
[29] Quiet Horse averted his gaze and casually brushed off the question.
[30] "Well, if you need to observe something, why not borrow my fishing gear? You can fish while observing, and there are often salmon in that area."
[31] Kurihara made a motion with his muscular arm, imitating casting a fishing rod. He is tall and muscular, with arms and legs twice as thick as Jingma's, and has a sturdy, dark complexion with a gentle, downcast expression. His appearance and cheerful character together create the genuine, wholesome aura of a healthy, rustic country man. During hunting season, he enters the mountains with a single-handed rifle. This time is no exception. Kurihara's boar and deer kills were turned into hotpot for dinner. He mentioned that he is married but has no children, and that his parents passed away. When Jingma first came, Kurihara and his wife, Akiko, took care of the household chores together, but Akiko fell ill a year ago and has been bedridden ever since, leaving Kurihara to manage things on his own.
[32] When Jingma heard this on his first day here, he expressed sympathy and said, "That's tough." Kurihara, however, laughed heartily and replied, "Actually, it's fortunate that the store is quiet, so it's not very strenuous. When a few customers come at once, the village folks come to help."
[33] "Fishing? I've never fished before."
[34] "Never?" Kurihara, who grew up in the village, seemed incredulous and widened his eyes, "But if you try, you'll find that fishing is surprisingly easy. I have a secret bait recipe. With artificial lures, you need various skills, but with edible bait, it's not so difficult. This summer, an elderly guest over sixty years old caught six salmon in two hours and was delighted. He said he hadn't fished since he was a child."
[35] Feeling that refusing would prolong the conversation, Jingma borrowed the fishing gear. After all, there was nothing to do today, and fishing might be a good way to pass the time.
[36] Jūmi took out the fishing gear from the house and gave Jirō a brief lesson on how to use it. He then added, "I'll make a dish out of the fish you catch tonight. Although it's past the fishing season, I promise it'll be delicious. You've been eating a lot of meat lately, so you must be getting tired of it. Anyway, with that bait, you'll be able to catch fish."
[37] He added, "You'll be able to catch fish even if you're clumsy," as if he was already thinking about how to prepare the fish.
[38] Jirō reluctantly shouldered the fishing gear with his right shoulder and headed towards the Dragon's Head in the winter sunlight. Once December arrives, the mountains turn gray, and the vibrant life force disappears. This is the season of "endurance," but Jirō began to wonder, "Do I really want to survive?"
[39] He walked along the narrow shortcut by the riverbank, starting from Gion-no-yu, heading north. After about fifteen minutes, he arrived at a slightly open area. The stream curved suddenly upstream, forming a pond, and the inside became a small riverbank. This place is called Dragon's Pond. Only the faint sound of the waterfall could be heard in the pond, and there was no human presence. Only the lonely cries of birds and the rustling of the needles could be heard in the wind.
[40]
[41] The branches stretched almost to the sky, and the inside of the pond, although it was a riverbank, was a place of rough stones rolling around. It was not a leisurely place to spread out a plastic sheet and have lunch. Moreover, on the outside of the pond, where the water flowed more rapidly, there was a cliff that stood upright like a knife, blocking the view. Behind the riverbank was the steep slope of the mountain, and the road to the upstream was cut off here, so the feeling of being in a dead end was very vivid.
[42] At the very back of the riverbank, facing the direction of the pond, there was a huge rock that rose from the slope of the mountain, pointing straight up to the sky. This rock, which seemed to suddenly appear from between the trees, was about four meters high, with its front end extending towards the pond at a certain angle. Due to the narrowness of the riverbank, it felt even stronger than its appearance suggested. This dark gray rock that dominated the surroundings was called the Dragon's Head.
[43] Although it was a rock with a width that could not be reached even by spreading one's arms, it tapered off neatly and smoothly towards the top, with only the front end slightly curved, extending horizontally towards the pond. It was said that its shape resembled a beheaded dragon and was named the Dragon's Head.
[44] In that case, it should be "Dragon's Body" rather than "Dragon's Head." However, according to the legend of the village, the dragon that had brought disaster to the village was killed, and its head turned into this rock. The head was buried under the rock.
[45] The lower part of the large rock was hollowed out, with a cavity about fifty centimeters high and thirty centimeters deep. From another angle, it could be interpreted as a shrine for the dragon's head. However, although it was a legendary relic, there were no sacred ropes or signs on the riverbank. Unless you had heard the story beforehand, people would probably walk by without paying any attention, thinking "It's just a strange rock."
[46] Jingma sat down on a suitable rock beside him and looked up at Dragon's Head. The sunlight that spilled through the branches blocking the sky cast dappled shadows on the rock surface, resembling dragon scales. Moreover, whenever the wind blew, the shadows would sway, making it look as if the headless dragon was still alive.
[47] He casually put his fishing tackle aside and, as he had done for the past three days, started from the left side and climbed up to the top of the rock. The soil was dry and slightly sticky, making it easy to climb up the slope. There have probably been many impolite climbers in the past. There are some small pits on the rock surface that feel quite nice and can be used as footholds. Since there are three large rocks tightly packed together on the right side of Dragon's Head, it is difficult to find a foothold, so the footprints for climbing are concentrated on the left side.
[48] The front end of Dragon's Head extends horizontally, and the top is flat, allowing one to sit on it comfortably. Due to its sufficient width and thickness, even when a person sits on it, it will not break.
[49] What if one falls from above? At first, Jingma simply had a sense of curiosity and tried climbing up. After climbing up, he found that it was unexpectedly delightful. As a result, he would leave the inn every afternoon and sit on this VIP seat until the sun set. Since the cliff is higher than the rock, the view is not good. However, the sense of being trapped and the open feeling of "only being able to advance towards the sky and having no other choice" towards the sky, he liked it very much. The winter wind blowing from the river occasionally brushed past his cheeks and collar, and the sunlight was surprisingly warm.
[50] ... It would be nice to wait for the first snowfall here. If it were here, one could wait calmly.
[51] He felt he had finally found a place to settle down. On this day, he gazed up at the sky as usual, but when the sound of a bird taking flight made him turn around, he noticed a light brown Western-style tower protruding from the trees on the slope behind him. The tower was not visible from the ground, and he had been so focused on looking in the direction of the pond that he only noticed it now. Although only the upper half of the tower was visible, it could be seen that a luxurious terrace extended towards this side under the Western-style conical roof. The distance was too far, so the details could not be seen. Judging by its location, it was probably a building of the Koto family.
[52] The Koto family is almost the owner of all the mountains in the village of Koto. It is said to be the descendants of the hero who defeated the dragon that Quietly rode on, and is still respected by the villagers. Koto's boss, Kureno, is also a distant relative of the Koto family.
[53] Quietly remembered what Kureno had said last night. Initially, the tower was built to monitor the dragon that was defeated. It was said to be an old-style watchtower that was replaced by the Western-style tower during the Taisho period.
[54] So, he had been sitting on such an important historical site, and if someone asked him about it, it could become a big problem. Suddenly, Quietly felt uneasy. He must avoid trouble, but this place was too pleasant, and he didn't want to give it up.
[55] "What are you doing there?"

[172] * * *
[173] Regimen: A straw rope hung in front of a shrine to indicate a prohibition or to bring good luck during the New Year.
[174] Water-dried and Uchiwaka: A type of traditional Japanese court garment called "kimono". Water-dried and kimono have the same origin, but the former was originally the daily attire of commoners. Unlike kimono, water-dried and kimono are reinforced and connected at the front and back seams with "chrysanthemum stitching". Additionally, water-dried and kimono do not have a neck collar like kimono, but are fastened at the neck with a thin belt. Over time, water-dried and kimono became the daily attire of samurai and some members of the imperial court, and eventually became a type of formal wear. Nowadays, female religious figures sometimes wear water-dried and kimono without chrysanthemum stitching.
[175] Utsunomiya: Utsunomiya is a Japanese historical figure, the ninth son of Yoshitsune, and a samurai from the Heian period. His childhood name was Utsunomiya, and he was born into the Uesugi clan.
[176] [4] Tabi: A type of Japanese short sock, with a divide between the big toe and the other toes, typically made of cotton. Tabi are often worn with Japanese traditional footwear such as geta and zori.

[789][1] Fukinuki: A common roof decoration in traditional East Asian architecture, similar to a canopy. It is believed to have originated from the Chinese architectural element of bifeng, which was introduced to Japan and evolved to become a prominent feature in many Japanese buildings. Fukinuki can be classified into Tange Fukinuki (からはふ), Chidori Fukinuki (ちどりはふ), Irimaya Fukinuki (いりもやはふ), and Kiritsuma Fukinuki (きりつまはふ) based on differences in line usage and building layout.
[790][2] Oniwa: Decorative roof tiles on the ridgepole or rafters, with patterns such as animal faces or lotus flowers. Oniwa is also called Oniwa even if it does not have a demonic face. The pattern used by the Kono family is a koto-shaped pattern.
[791][3] "Mark 3": A home video game console released by Sega (SEGA) on October 20, 1985.

[939] [1] Toward-bent: the part of the roof of a shrine hall or a temple facing the main staircase, protruding.
[940] [2] Hitori-no-miya: a type of noble residence that emerged in the Heian period, with a main house called the "dormitory" and its east, west, and north annexes connected by a covered corridor called the "hitori-no-miya." This type of residence has since been simplified.
[941][3] Sanwa Soil: Chinese "sanhe nü," a mixture of mud, lime, and water pounded into a solid mass. Named after the three materials mixed, it refers to the "soil" made of sanwa soil in the text. In traditional Japanese homes, people's living spaces are divided into two parts: the elevated, boarded part above ground, and the part at ground level. The latter is the "soil," typically located at the entrance between the interior and the exterior. In the past, the soil was used for household chores or cooking, so it was quite spacious. However, in modern homes, the soil has become narrow and serves only as a place to change shoes, which is what we commonly refer to as the "entrance" part.
[942][4] Tsubo: A Japanese unit of area, equivalent to approximately 1.62 square meters.
